### [1] [Internalized Reasoning for Long-Context Visual Document Understanding](https://arxiv.org/abs/2604.02371)
*Austin Veselka*

Main category: cs.CV

TL;DR: Synthesized reasoning for long-document understanding via synthetic thinking traces and internalized prompting; performs better than larger models on MMLongBenchDoc; uses <think>/<cot> prompts and low-strength model merging, evaluated on Qwen3 VL 32B and Mistral 3.1-24B; pipeline released.


<details>
  <summary>Details</summary>
Motivation: Open-source visual long-document models underexplore reasoning capabilities; introducing synthetic reasoning traces and internalization to boost performance while enabling efficiency and reproducibility.

Method: Generate per-page relevance scores, extract textual evidence, and order traces; apply supervised fine-tuning on the traces within <think> tags gated by a <cot> control token; internalize reasoning via low-strength model merging; evaluate on MMLongBenchDoc and MMLBD-C across Qwen3 VL 32B and Mistral Small 3.1 24B; release pipeline.

Result: Qwen3 VL 32B achieves 58.3 on MMLongBenchDoc, beating a 7× larger Qwen3 VL 235B A22B (57.0). Mistral results show synthetic reasoning outperforms distillation from the Thinking traces by 3.8 points on MMLBD-C; internalized reasoning yields 12.4× fewer mean output tokens vs explicit reasoning.

Conclusion: Synthetic reasoning via synthetic traces and internalized prompting improves open-model performance on long-document tasks; approach enables efficiency gains and reproducibility through a released pipeline.

Abstract: Visual long-document understanding is critical for enterprise, legal, and scientific applications, yet the best performing open recipes have not explored reasoning, a capability which has driven leaps in math and code performance. We introduce a synthetic data pipeline for reasoning in long-document understanding that generates thinking traces by scoring each page for question relevance, extracting textual evidence and ordering it from most to least relevant. We apply SFT to the resulting traces within \texttt{<think>} tags, gated by a \texttt{<cot>} control token, and the resulting reasoning capability is internalized via low-strength model merging. We study Qwen3 VL 32B and Mistral Small 3.1 24B. With Qwen3 VL, we achieve 58.3 on MMLongBenchDoc, surpassing the 7$\times$ larger Qwen3 VL 235B A22B (57.0). With Mistral, we show that synthetic reasoning outperforms distillation from the Thinking version's traces by 3.8 points on MMLBD-C, and internalized reasoning exhibits 12.4$\times$ fewer mean output tokens compared to explicit reasoning. We release our pipeline for reproducibility and further exploration.

</details>


### [2] [Beyond Fixed Inference: Quantitative Flow Matching for Adaptive Image Denoising](https://arxiv.org/abs/2604.02392)
*Jigang Duan,Genwei Ma,Xu Jiang,Wenfeng Xu,Ping Yang,Xing Zhao*

Main category: cs.CV

TL;DR: Quantitative flow matching for adaptive image denoising that estimates noise level from local statistics and adapts inference trajectory (start, steps, step-size) to match corruption level, improving accuracy and efficiency across varying noise conditions.


<details>
  <summary>Details</summary>
Motivation: Denoising with unknown, varying noise is challenging because learned vector fields may be inconsistent across noise levels, causing degraded restoration when training and inference conditions mismatch.

Method: Estimate input noise from local pixel statistics; use this estimate to adapt the inference trajectory in a diffusion/flow-based model, including starting point, number of steps, and step-size schedule; couple noise estimation with noise-adaptive flow inference.

Result: Improved restoration accuracy and inference efficiency; robust generalization across natural, medical, and microscopy images under diverse noise levels and imaging conditions.

Conclusion: Quantitative noise estimation integrated with adaptive flow inference yields robust, efficient denoising across varying noise conditions and imaging modalities.

Abstract: Diffusion and flow-based generative models have shown strong potential for image restoration. However, image denoising under unknown and varying noise conditions remains challenging, because the learned vector fields may become inconsistent across different noise levels, leading to degraded restoration quality under mismatch between training and inference. To address this issue, we propose a quantitative flow matching framework for adaptive image denoising. The method first estimates the input noise level from local pixel statistics, and then uses this quantitative estimate to adapt the inference trajectory, including the starting point, the number of integration steps, and the step-size schedule. In this way, the denoising process is better aligned with the actual corruption level of each input, reducing unnecessary computation for lightly corrupted images while providing sufficient refinement for heavily degraded ones. By coupling quantitative noise estimation with noise-adaptive flow inference, the proposed method improves both restoration accuracy and inference efficiency. Extensive experiments on natural, medical, and microscopy images demonstrate its robustness and strong generalization across diverse noise levels and imaging conditions.

</details>


### [3] [Environment-Aware Channel Prediction for Vehicular Communications: A Multimodal Visual Feature Fusion Framework](https://arxiv.org/abs/2604.02396)
*Xuejian Zhang,Ruisi He,Minseok Kim,Inocent Calist,Mi Yang,Ziyi Qi*

Main category: cs.CV

TL;DR: An environment-aware, multimodal fusion framework jointly predicts PL, DS, ASA, ASD, and APS for urban V2I, using GPS, panoramic RGB, semantic segmentation, and depth cues with a squeeze-excitation fusion module, achieving state-of-the-art RMSE and APS cosine similarities.


<details>
  <summary>Details</summary>
Motivation: 6G envisions integrated communication, sensing, and intelligence; environment-aware channel prediction is crucial for reliability, latency, and adaptability in vehicular channels. Traditional models struggle to generalize and deploy in diverse environments despite sensor data availability.

Method: A three-branch architecture fuses multimodal features (GPS, panoramic RGB, semantic segmentation, depth) via a squeeze-excitation attention gating module. For 360-D APS, a dedicated regression head with a composite multi-constraint loss enables joint prediction of PL, DS, ASA, ASD, and APS.

Result: On a synchronized urban V2I dataset, achieves PL RMSE 3.26 dB; DS 37.66 ns; ASA 5.05°; ASD 5.08°; APS mean/median cosine similarities 0.9342/0.9571; indicating strong accuracy and generalization for practical 6G channel prediction.

Conclusion: The framework demonstrates accurate, generalizable, and practically viable environment-aware channel prediction in vehicular networks, enabling improved planning for future 6G systems.

Abstract: The deep integration of communication with intelligence and sensing, as a defining vision of 6G, renders environment-aware channel prediction a key enabling technology. As a representative 6G application, vehicular communications require accurate and forward-looking channel prediction under stringent reliability, latency, and adaptability demands. Traditional empirical and deterministic models remain limited in balancing accuracy, generalization, and deployability, while the growing availability of onboard and roadside sensing devices offers a promising source of environmental priors. This paper proposes an environment-aware channel prediction framework based on multimodal visual feature fusion. Using GPS data and vehicle-side panoramic RGB images, together with semantic segmentation and depth estimation, the framework extracts semantic, depth, and position features through a three-branch architecture and performs adaptive multimodal fusion via a squeeze-excitation attention gating module. For 360-dimensional angular power spectrum (APS) prediction, a dedicated regression head and a composite multi-constraint loss are further designed. As a result, joint prediction of path loss (PL), delay spread (DS), azimuth spread of arrival (ASA), azimuth spread of departure (ASD), and APS is achieved. Experiments on a synchronized urban V2I measurement dataset yield the best root mean square error (RMSE) of 3.26 dB for PL, RMSEs of 37.66 ns, 5.05 degrees, and 5.08 degrees for DS, ASA, and ASD, respectively, and mean/median APS cosine similarities of 0.9342/0.9571, demonstrating strong accuracy, generalization, and practical potential for intelligent channel prediction in 6G vehicular communications.

</details>


### [4] [Variational Encoder--Multi-Decoder (VE-MD) for Privacy-by-functional-design (Group) Emotion Recognition](https://arxiv.org/abs/2604.02397)
*Anderson Augusma,Dominique Vaufreydaz,Fédérique Letué*

Main category: cs.CV

TL;DR: A privacy-aware variational encoder-multi-decoder framework (VE-MD) for group emotion recognition that uses structural supervision to preserve interaction cues and avoid per-person outputs, achieving SOTA on GAF-3.0 and VGAF and competitive results on IER datasets when fused with audio.


<details>
  <summary>Details</summary>
Motivation: Address privacy concerns in GER by avoiding explicit individual monitoring while leveraging structural representations to capture group interactions; distinguish GER from IER and show that latent-only optimization harms interaction cues.

Method: Variational encoder with multiple decoders: transformer-based PersonQuery decoder or dense heatmap decoder; joint optimization for emotion classification and prediction of body/face structure; structural outputs used as supervision; experiments across six datasets; multimodal fusion with audio for IER.

Result: Structural supervision improves representation learning; latent-space optimization alone may hurt GER; VE-MD achieves state-of-the-art on GAF-3.0 (90.06%) and VGAF (82.25% with audio); outperforms SOTA on SamSemo with added text; competitive on MER-MULTI, DFEW, EngageNet.

Conclusion: Preserving interaction-related structural information is beneficial for group-level affect modeling without per-person features; structural outputs function as denoising for IER; VE-MD provides privacy-aware GER with strong performance.

Abstract: Group Emotion Recognition (GER) aims to infer collective affect in social environments such as classrooms, crowds, and public events. Many existing approaches rely on explicit individual-level processing, including cropped faces, person tracking, or per-person feature extraction, which makes the analysis pipeline person-centric and raises privacy concerns in deployment scenarios where only group-level understanding is needed. This research proposes VE-MD, a Variational Encoder-Multi-Decoder framework for group emotion recognition under a privacy-aware functional design. Rather than providing formal anonymization or cryptographic privacy guarantees, VE-MD is designed to avoid explicit individual monitoring by constraining the model to predict only aggregate group-level affect, without identity recognition or per-person emotion outputs. VE-MD learns a shared latent representation jointly optimized for emotion classification and internal prediction of body and facial structural representations. Two structural decoding strategies are investigated: a transformer-based PersonQuery decoder and a dense Heatmap decoder that naturally accommodates variable group sizes. Experiments on six in-the-wild datasets, including two GER and four Individual Emotion Recognition (IER) benchmarks, show that structural supervision consistently improves representation learning. More importantly, the results reveal a clear distinction between GER and IER: optimizing the latent space alone is often insufficient for GER because it tends to attenuate interaction-related cues, whereas preserving explicit structural outputs improves collective affect inference. In contrast, projected structural representations seem to act as an effective denoising bottleneck for IER. VE-MD achieves state-of-the-art performance on GAF-3.0 (up to 90.06%) and VGAF (82.25% with multimodal fusion with audio). These results show that preserving interaction-related structural information is particularly beneficial for group-level affect modeling without relying on prior individual feature extraction. On IER datasets using multimodal fusion with audio modality, VE-MD outperforms SOTA on SamSemo (77.9%, adding text modality) while achieving competitive performances on MER-MULTI (63.8%), DFEW (70.7%) and EngageNet (69.0).

</details>


### [5] [LumiVideo: An Intelligent Agentic System for Video Color Grading](https://arxiv.org/abs/2604.02409)
*Yuchen Guo,Junli Gong,Hongmin Cai,Yiu-ming Cheung,Weifeng Su*

Main category: cs.CV

TL;DR: A pipeline-structured, interpretable auto color-grading system (LumiVideo) that mimics professional colorists through Perception, Reasoning, Execution, and Reflection, using LLMs with RAG/Tree of Thoughts to derive ASC-CDL configs and a global 3D LUT from raw log video; includes a log-encoded video benchmark (LumiGrade) and supports optional user feedback; achieves near-expert quality automatically and offers precise iterative control.


<details>
  <summary>Details</summary>
Motivation: To overcome the lack of interpretability and iterative control in existing automated color-grading methods by modeling the professional colorist workflow as an agentic system that outputs parameterized, auditable color adjustments rather than direct pixels.

Method: A four-stage agentic pipeline: (1) Perception analyzes scene lighting and semantics from raw log footage; (2) Reasoning uses a large language model with retrieval-augmented generation and Tree of Thoughts to explore color parameter space; (3) Execution translates deduced parameters into industry-standard ASC-CDL configurations and a temporally consistent global 3D LUT; (4) Reflection allows optional natural language feedback for refinement. Introduces LumiGrade as a benchmark for log-encoded video grading.

Result: LumiVideo approaches human expert quality in fully automatic mode and preserves precise iterative control when guided by user input; the approach guarantees temporal consistency through analytic parameter-to-pipeline translation.

Conclusion: An interpretable, controllable, and high-quality automatic color-grading system that aligns with professional workflows, reinforced by a standardized benchmark (LumiGrade) for evaluation.

Abstract: Video color grading is a critical post-production process that transforms flat, log-encoded raw footage into emotionally resonant cinematic visuals. Existing automated methods act as static, black-box executors that directly output edited pixels, lacking both interpretability and the iterative control required by professionals. We introduce LumiVideo, an agentic system that mimics the cognitive workflow of professional colorists through four stages: Perception, Reasoning, Execution, and Reflection. Given only raw log video, LumiVideo autonomously produces a cinematic base grade by analyzing the scene's physical lighting and semantic content. Its Reasoning engine synergizes an LLM's internalized cinematic knowledge with a Retrieval-Augmented Generation (RAG) framework via a Tree of Thoughts (ToT) search to navigate the non-linear color parameter space. Rather than generating pixels, the system compiles the deduced parameters into industry-standard ASC-CDL configurations and a globally consistent 3D LUT, analytically guaranteeing temporal consistency. An optional Reflection loop then allows creators to refine the result via natural language feedback. We further introduce LumiGrade, the first log-encoded video benchmark for evaluating automated grading. Experiments show that LumiVideo approaches human expert quality in fully automatic mode while enabling precise iterative control when directed.

</details>


### [6] [From Elevation Maps To Contour Lines: SVM and Decision Trees to Detect Violin Width Reduction](https://arxiv.org/abs/2604.02446)
*Philémon Beghin,Anne-Emmanuelle Ceulemans,François Glineur*

Main category: cs.CV

TL;DR: Contour-based features outperform elevation-map-based raw features for detecting violin width reduction; both SVM and Decision Trees are evaluated.


<details>
  <summary>Details</summary>
Motivation: Evaluate whether 3D photogrammetric geometry representations (elevation maps vs parametric contour features) improve automatic detection of violin width reduction using ML classifiers.

Method: Build two input representations from 3D data: (1) geometry-based raw features from elevation maps; (2) engineered features via parametric contour line fitting. Train and evaluate SVM and Decision Tree classifiers on both.

Result: Elevation-map features occasionally yield strong results but do not exceed contour-based features; contour-based inputs provide superior performance.

Conclusion: Contour-based feature engineering is more effective than raw elevation-map representations for detecting violin width reduction from 3D data; both SVM and Decision Trees benefit from engineered contour features.

Abstract: We explore the automatic detection of violin width reduction using 3D photogrammetric meshes. We compare SVM and Decision Trees applied to a geometry-based raw representation built from elevation maps with a more targeted, feature-engineered approach relying on parametric contour lines fitting. Although elevation maps occasionally achieve strong results, their performance does not surpass that of the contour-based inputs.

</details>


### [7] [PlayGen-MoG: Framework for Diverse Multi-Agent Play Generation via Mixture-of-Gaussians Trajectory Prediction](https://arxiv.org/abs/2604.02447)
*Kevin Song*

Main category: cs.CV

TL;DR: A formation-conditioned generation framework (PlayGen-MoG) using a Mixture-of-Gaussians head, relative spatial attention, and non-autoregressive displacement prediction to generate diverse football plays from a single formation; achieves low ADE/FDE and high mixture utilization without mode collapse.


<details>
  <summary>Details</summary>
Motivation: Capture the diversity and coordination of team sports plays while enabling generation from a single static formation, addressing issues in CVAE/diffusion-based methods and forecast-regime requirements.

Method: Three design choices: (1) Mixture-of-Gaussians output head with shared mixture weights across all agents to select a single play scenario coupling all players' trajectories; (2) relative spatial attention encoding pairwise positions and distances as learned attention biases; (3) non-autoregressive prediction of absolute displacements from the initial formation, removing history dependence and drift.

Result: On American football tracking data, achieves 1.68 yard ADE and 3.98 yard FDE; maintains full utilization of all 8 mixture components with entropy 2.06/2.08; qualitatively demonstrates diverse generation without mode collapse.

Conclusion: PlayGen-MoG offers an extensible, formation-conditioned framework that mitigates posterior collapse and history-dependence, delivering diverse, realistic plays from a single formation and enabling broader use in play design.

Abstract: Multi-agent trajectory generation in team sports requires models that capture both the diversity of possible plays and realistic spatial coordination between players on plays. Standard generative approaches such as Conditional Variational Autoencoders (CVAE) and diffusion models struggle with this task, exhibiting posterior collapse or convergence to the dataset mean. Moreover, most trajectory prediction methods operate in a forecasting regime that requires multiple frames of observed history, limiting their use for play design where only the initial formation is available. We present PlayGen-MoG, an extensible framework for formation-conditioned play generation that addresses these challenges through three design choices: 1/ a Mixture-of-Gaussians (MoG) output head with shared mixture weights across all agents, where a single set of weights selects a play scenario that couples all players' trajectories, 2/ relative spatial attention that encodes pairwise player positions and distances as learned attention biases, and 3/ non-autoregressive prediction of absolute displacements from the initial formation, eliminating cumulative error drift and removing the dependence on observed trajectory history, enabling realistic play generation from a single static formation alone. On American football tracking data, PlayGen-MoG achieves 1.68 yard ADE and 3.98 yard FDE while maintaining full utilization of all 8 mixture components with entropy of 2.06 out of 2.08, and qualitatively confirming diverse generation without mode collapse.

</details>


### [8] [Street-Legal Physical-World Adversarial Rim for License Plates](https://arxiv.org/abs/2604.02457)
*Nikhil Kalidasu,Sahana Ganapathy*

Main category: cs.CV

TL;DR: White-box, physically realizable adversarial attack on an open-source ALPR (SPAR) claiming street-legal viability in Texas; reduces recognition by 60% and enables 18% targeted impersonation at < $100, highlighting both practicality and defense needs.


<details>
  <summary>Details</summary>
Motivation: Evaluate the real-world practicality and legality of physically adversarial attacks on license plate recognition to inform defense strategies and policy considerations.

Method: Design and evaluation of a street-legal physical adversarial rim (SPAR) that does not require ALPR infrastructure access, does not obscure the attacker’s plate, targets the fast-alpr system, and uses cost-effective, commodity tools under controlled conditions (white-box setting).

Result: Under optimal conditions, ALPR accuracy is reduced by 60% with an 18% rate of targeted impersonation; production cost is under $100; demonstrated using commercial coding tools.

Conclusion: ALPR systems can be vulnerable to practical, low-cost physical adversarial attacks under realistic conditions, necessitating improved defenses, broader evaluation across systems, and careful consideration of legal/ethical implications and policy responses.

Abstract: Automatic license plate reader (ALPR) systems are widely deployed to identify and track vehicles. While prior work has demonstrated vulnerabilities in ALPR systems, far less attention has been paid to their legality and physical-world practicality. We investigate whether low-resourced threat actors can engineer a successful adversarial attack against a modern open-source ALPR system. We introduce the Street-legal Physical Adversarial Rim (SPAR), a physically realizable white-box attack against the popular ALPR system fast-alpr. SPAR requires no access to ALPR infrastructure during attack deployment and does not alter or obscure the attacker's license plate. Based on prior legislation and case law, we argue that SPAR is street-legal in the state of Texas. Under optimal conditions, SPAR reduces ALPR accuracy by 60% and achieves an 18% targeted impersonation rate. SPAR can be produced for under $100, and it was implemented entirely by commercial agentic coding assistants. These results highlight practical vulnerabilities in modern ALPR systems under realistic physical-world conditions and suggest new directions for both attack and defense.

</details>


### [9] [VERTIGO: Visual Preference Optimization for Cinematic Camera Trajectory Generation](https://arxiv.org/abs/2604.02467)
*Mengtian Li,Yuwei Lu,Feifei Li,Chenqi Gan,Zhifeng Xie,Xi Wang*

Main category: cs.CV

TL;DR: VERTIGO introduces visual preference optimization for camera trajectory generators by rendering motion previews in Unity, scoring them with a cinematically tuned vision-language model via cyclic semantic similarity, and applying Direct Preference Optimization (DPO) post-training to improve framing, consistency, and aesthetics, notably reducing off-screen characters from 38% to ~0%.


<details>
  <summary>Details</summary>
Motivation: Generative camera systems currently lack a 'director-in-the-loop' and explicit supervision for visual desirability, yielding natural but poorly framed or off-screen content; there is a need for explicit visual preference signals to steer camera trajectories.

Method: Render 2D previews from generated camera motions in Unity; score previews using a cinematically fine-tuned vision-language model through a cyclic semantic similarity mechanism to align renders with text prompts; use these signals for Direct Preference Optimization (DPO) during post-training of camera trajectory generators.

Result: Quantitative and user studies on Unity renders and diffusion-based Camera-to-Video pipelines show consistent gains in adherence to constraints, framing quality, and perceptual realism; off-screen character rate drops from 38% to near 0%; preserves geometric fidelity of camera motion; users prefer VERTIGO over baselines for composition, consistency, prompt adherence, and aesthetic quality.

Conclusion: Visual preference post-training with VERTIGO effectively aligns camera trajectory generation with human aesthetic preferences, delivering improved framing and perceptual realism while maintaining motion fidelity; demonstrates a practical pipeline combining real-time rendering, vision-language scoring, and DPO.

Abstract: Cinematic camera control relies on a tight feedback loop between director and cinematographer, where camera motion and framing are continuously reviewed and refined. Recent generative camera systems can produce diverse, text-conditioned trajectories, but they lack this "director in the loop" and have no explicit supervision of whether a shot is visually desirable. This results in in-distribution camera motion but poor framing, off-screen characters, and undesirable visual aesthetics. In this paper, we introduce VERTIGO, the first framework for visual preference optimization of camera trajectory generators. Our framework leverages a real-time graphics engine (Unity) to render 2D visual previews from generated camera motion. A cinematically fine-tuned vision-language model then scores these previews using our proposed cyclic semantic similarity mechanism, which aligns renders with text prompts. This process provides the visual preference signals for Direct Preference Optimization (DPO) post-training. Both quantitative evaluations and user studies on Unity renders and diffusion-based Camera-to-Video pipelines show consistent gains in condition adherence, framing quality, and perceptual realism. Notably, VERTIGO reduces the character off-screen rate from 38% to nearly 0% while preserving the geometric fidelity of camera motion. User study participants further prefer VERTIGO over baselines across composition, consistency, prompt adherence, and aesthetic quality, confirming the perceptual benefits of our visual preference post-training.

</details>


### [10] [Hierarchical, Interpretable, Label-Free Concept Bottleneck Model](https://arxiv.org/abs/2604.02468)
*Haodong Xie,Yujun Cai,Rahul Singh Maharjan,Yiwei Wang,Federico Tavella,Angelo Cangelosi*

Main category: cs.CV

TL;DR: Proposes HIL-CBM, a hierarchical, label-free concept bottleneck model with gradient-based visual consistency loss and dual abstraction-level classifiers, achieving improved accuracy and interpretability over sparse CBMs without relational concept annotations.


<details>
  <summary>Details</summary>
Motivation: Address the limitation of single-level semantics in existing CBMs by modeling concepts at multiple abstraction levels, to better mimic human cognitive processing and produce more aligned, hierarchical explanations without requiring relational annotations.

Method: Introduce hierarchical concept abstraction with two classification heads corresponding to different concept abstraction levels. Employ a gradient-based visual consistency loss to align spatial attention across abstraction layers, encouraging consistent abstraction. Train without relational concept annotations (label-free concepts) while providing multi-level explanations.

Result: Empirically outperforms state-of-the-art sparse CBMs in classification accuracy on benchmark datasets. Human evaluations indicate that explanations are more interpretable and accurate, and that the model maintains a hierarchical, label-free approach to concept definitions.

Conclusion: HIL-CBM demonstrates that hierarchical, label-free concept bottleneck models can improve both predictive performance and interpretability by aligning concept abstraction with model predictions, offering multi-level explanations without needing relational concept supervision.

Abstract: Concept Bottleneck Models (CBMs) introduce interpretability to black-box deep learning models by predicting labels through human-understandable concepts. However, unlike humans, who identify objects at different levels of abstraction using both general and specific features, existing CBMs operate at a single semantic level in both concept and label space. We propose HIL-CBM, a Hierarchical Interpretable Label-Free Concept Bottleneck Model that extends CBMs into a hierarchical framework to enhance interpretability by more closely mirroring the human cognitive process. HIL-CBM enables classification and explanation across multiple semantic levels without requiring relational concept annotations. HIL-CBM aligns the abstraction level of concept-based explanations with that of model predictions, progressing from abstract to concrete. This is achieved by (i) introducing a gradient-based visual consistency loss that encourages abstraction layers to focus on similar spatial regions, and (ii) training dual classification heads, each operating on feature concepts at different abstraction levels. Experiments on benchmark datasets demonstrate that HIL-CBM outperforms state-of-the-art sparse CBMs in classification accuracy. Human evaluations further show that HIL-CBM provides more interpretable and accurate explanations, while maintaining a hierarchical and label-free approach to feature concepts.

</details>


### [11] [Guideline2Graph: Profile-Aware Multimodal Parsing for Executable Clinical Decision Graphs](https://arxiv.org/abs/2604.02477)
*Onur Selim Kilic,Yeti Z. Gurbuz,Cem O. Yaldiz,Afra Nawar,Etrit Haxholli,Ogul Can,Eli Waxman*

Main category: cs.CV

TL;DR: A decomposition-first pipeline converts full clinical guidelines into executable decision graphs using topology-aware chunking, interface-constrained graph generation, and provenance-preserving aggregation, yielding substantial improvements in graph quality over existing methods on a prostate-guideline benchmark.


<details>
  <summary>Details</summary>
Motivation: Long, multimodal guidelines with branching recommendations are hard to convert into executable CDS, and cross-page continuity is easy to break with one-shot parsing; current extractors are local and fail to build coherent, auditable decision graphs across whole documents.

Method: Decompose evidence into topology-aware chunks, constrain graph generation via interface definitions, and perform provenance-preserving global aggregation to assemble a complete decision graph. The approach uses explicit entry/terminal interfaces and semantic deduplication to maintain cross-page continuity and auditable control flow, rather than relying on single-pass generation.

Result: On a matched-input prostate-guideline benchmark with a common VLM backbone, the complete merged graph shows edge precision/recall improving from 19.6%/16.1% to 69.0%/87.5%, and node recall improving from 78.1% to 93.8%.

Conclusion: Decomposition-first, auditable guideline-to-CDS conversion is effective on the tested benchmark, though validation is currently limited to a single adjudicated prostate guideline and broader multi-guideline validation is warranted.

Abstract: Clinical practice guidelines are long, multimodal documents whose branching recommendations are difficult to convert into executable clinical decision support (CDS), and one-shot parsing often breaks cross-page continuity. Recent LLM/VLM extractors are mostly local or text-centric, under-specifying section interfaces and failing to consolidate cross-page control flow across full documents into one coherent decision graph. We present a decomposition-first pipeline that converts full-guideline evidence into an executable clinical decision graph through topology-aware chunking, interface-constrained chunk graph generation, and provenance-preserving global aggregation. Rather than relying on single-pass generation, the pipeline uses explicit entry/terminal interfaces and semantic deduplication to preserve cross-page continuity while keeping the induced control flow auditable and structurally consistent. We evaluate on an adjudicated prostate-guideline benchmark with matched inputs and the same underlying VLM backbone across compared methods. On the complete merged graph, our approach improves edge and triplet precision/recall from $19.6\%/16.1\%$ in existing models to $69.0\%/87.5\%$, while node recall rises from $78.1\%$ to $93.8\%$. These results support decomposition-first, auditable guideline-to-CDS conversion on this benchmark, while current evidence remains limited to one adjudicated prostate guideline and motivates broader multi-guideline validation.

</details>


### [12] [Generating Satellite Imagery Data for Wildfire Detection through Mask-Conditioned Generative AI](https://arxiv.org/abs/2604.02479)
*Valeria Martin,K. Brent Venable,Derek Morgan*

Main category: cs.CV

TL;DR: Diffusion-based EO foundation model (EarthSynth) can synthesize post-wildfire Sentinel-2 RGB imagery conditioned on burn masks without retraining; inpainting with pre-fire context outperforms full-tile generation; VLM-assisted prompts are competitive; color matching improves color realism but may lower saliency.


<details>
  <summary>Details</summary>
Motivation: Address the scarcity of labeled satellite imagery for DL wildfire monitoring by exploring synthetic data generation with a foundation model in EO, potentially enabling data augmentation without task-specific retraining.

Method: Evaluate six configurations varying (i) pipeline: mask-only full generation vs. inpainting with pre-fire context; (ii) prompt strategy: three hand-crafted prompts plus a VLM-generated prompt via Qwen2-VL; (iii) a region-wise color-matching post-processing step. Burn masks from CalFireSeg-50; 10 stratified test samples; metrics: Burn IoU, burn-region color distance (ΔC_burn), Darkness Contrast, Spectral Plausibility.

Result: Inpainting-based pipelines consistently outperform full-tile generation across metrics. The structured inpainting prompt yields best spatial alignment (Burn IoU = 0.456) and burn saliency (Darkness Contrast = 20.44). Color matching yields lowest ΔC_burn = 63.22 but reduces saliency. VLM-assisted inpainting is competitive with hand-crafted prompts.

Conclusion: The study supports using generative data augmentation via diffusion-based EO models for wildfire detection pipelines, enabling realistic post-fire imagery conditioning on burn masks without retraining; code and experiments are publicly available.

Abstract: The scarcity of labeled satellite imagery remains a fundamental bottleneck for deep-learning (DL)-based wildfire monitoring systems. This paper investigates whether a diffusion-based foundation model for Earth Observation (EO), EarthSynth, can synthesize realistic post-wildfire Sentinel-2 RGB imagery conditioned on existing burn masks, without task-specific retraining.
  Using burn masks derived from the CalFireSeg-50 dataset (Martin et al., 2025), we design and evaluate six controlled experimental configurations that systematically vary: (i) pipeline architecture (mask-only full generation vs. inpainting with pre-fire context), (ii) prompt engineering strategy (three hand-crafted prompts and a VLM-generated prompt via Qwen2-VL), and (iii) a region-wise color-matching post-processing step.
  Quantitative assessment on 10 stratified test samples uses four complementary metrics: Burn IoU, burn-region color distance (ΔC_burn), Darkness Contrast, and Spectral Plausibility. Results show that inpainting-based pipelines consistently outperform full-tile generation across all metrics, with the structured inpainting prompt achieving the best spatial alignment (Burn IoU = 0.456) and burn saliency (Darkness Contrast = 20.44), while color matching produces the lowest color distance (ΔC_burn = 63.22) at the cost of reduced burn saliency.
  VLM-assisted inpainting is competitive with hand-crafted prompts. These findings provide a foundation for incorporating generative data augmentation into wildfire detection pipelines.
  Code and experiments are available at: https://www.kaggle.com/code/valeriamartinh/genai-all-runned

</details>


### [13] [VLMs Need Words: Vision Language Models Ignore Visual Detail In Favor of Semantic Anchors](https://arxiv.org/abs/2604.02486)
*Haz Sameen Shahgir,Xiaofu Chen,Yu Fu,Erfan Shayegani,Nael Abu-Ghazaleh,Yova Kementchedjhieva,Yue Dong*

Main category: cs.CV

TL;DR: VLMs struggle on fine-grained visual tasks because training emphasizes mapping visual information into the textual space, causing reliance on nameable entities; providing arbitrary names helps, but task-specific finetuning yields stronger generalization, suggesting failures arise from learned shortcuts rather than architectural limits.


<details>
  <summary>Details</summary>
Motivation: Diagnose why Vision-Language Models underperform on fine-grained visual perception and matching tasks, and whether their training biases toward text mapping limit their reasoning about unnameable or novel visual entities.

Method: Benchmark VLMs on visual correspondence tasks (semantic, shape, face); use Logit Lens to inspect explicit semantic labeling of entities; test with arbitrary naming for unknown entities; compare zero-shot, nameable vs unnameable, and finetuned performance; evaluate task-specific finetuning versus language-prior exploitation.

Conclusion: Current VLM failures on visual tasks stem from learned shortcuts via training rather than fundamental architectural limitations; adjusting training to reduce reliance on language priors and/or enhance vision-centric representations can improve capability, with arbitrary naming offering a partial, non-solution and finetuning offering stronger gains.

Abstract: Vision Language Models (VLMs) achieve impressive performance across a wide range of multimodal tasks. However, on some tasks that demand fine-grained visual perception, they often fail even when the required information is present in their internal representations. In this work, we demonstrate that this gap arises from their narrow training pipeline which focuses on moving visual information to the textual space. Consequently, VLMs can only reason about visual entities that can be mapped to known concepts in the language space, leaving vision-focused tasks such as visual correspondence and reasoning about novel visual entities poorly supported. As a result, VLMs are severely limited in several important multimodal capabilities because they rely on brittle, hallucinated textual descriptions of visual entities that they cannot map to textual representations. We verify this behavior through visual correspondence tasks, in which VLMs must detect matching entities between two images. Testing across semantic, shape, and face correspondence tasks, we find that VLMs perform much better when the relevant entities are nameable in language than when they are unnameable. Mechanistically, our Logit Lens analyses confirm that VLMs explicitly assign semantic labels to nameable entities and surface more unique corresponding tokens compared to unnameable entities. Furthermore, we show that teaching completely arbitrary names for unknown entities improves performance, yet task-specific finetuning yields even stronger generalization without relying on language priors. Our findings suggest that current VLM failures on visual tasks reflect learned shortcuts from their training, rather than a fundamental limitation of multimodal architectures.

Central to our approach is Delaunay Graph Scoring, which not only reconstructs the underlying geometric manifold but also yields region-wise curvature signatures to robustly guide the reconstruction. Built on this foundation, our corner and wire selection modules leverage the Delaunay-induced prior to focus on highly probable elements, thereby shaping the search space and enabling accurate prediction even in previously intractable regions. ### [18] [Feature Attribution Stability Suite: How Stable Are Post-Hoc Attributions?](https://arxiv.org/abs/2604.02532)
*Kamalasankari Subramaniakuppusamy,Jugal Gajjar*

Main category: cs.CV

TL;DR: Introduces FASS, a benchmark for stable post-hoc feature attributions under realistic perturbations with a prediction-invariance filter; decomposes stability into structural similarity, rank correlation, and top-k Jaccard across geometric, photometric, and compression perturbations; finds geometric perturbations more destabilizing, conditioning on predictions reduces fragility, and Grad-CAM generally yields the highest stability.


<details>
  <summary>Details</summary>
Motivation: Current post-hoc attribution methods often fail to be stable under input perturbations, and existing metrics neglect prediction preservation, conflating model sensitivity with explanation fragility. A benchmark enforcing prediction invariance and analyzing stability across perturbation families is needed.

Method: Define the Feature Attribution Stability Suite (FASS) with prediction-invariance filtering. Compute three complementary metrics—structural similarity, rank correlation, top-k Jaccard overlap—over geometric, photometric, and compression perturbations. Result: Stability depends on perturbation family and the prediction-preservation filter. Geometric perturbations reveal far greater attribution instability than photometric changes; without forcing prediction preservation, up to 99% of evaluation pairs change predictions. Grad-CAM achieves the highest stability across datasets; method-level trends are consistent.

Conclusion: FASS provides a controlled framework to assess attribution stability, revealing that perturbation type and prediction-invariance filtering critically shape stability estimates. It enables fair cross-method evaluation and highlights Grad-CAM as comparatively more stable among the tested methods.

Abstract: Post-hoc feature attribution methods are widely deployed in safety-critical vision systems, yet their stability under realistic input perturbations remains poorly characterized. Existing metrics evaluate explanations primarily under additive noise, collapse stability to a single scalar, and fail to condition on prediction preservation, conflating explanation fragility with model sensitivity. We introduce the Feature Attribution Stability Suite (FASS), a benchmark that enforces prediction-invariance filtering, decomposes stability into three complementary metrics: structural similarity, rank correlation, and top-k Jaccard overlap-and evaluates across geometric, photometric, and compression perturbations. Evaluating four attribution methods (Integrated Gradients, GradientSHAP, Grad-CAM, LIME) across four architectures and three datasets-ImageNet-1K, MS COCO, and CIFAR-10, FASS shows that stability estimates depend critically on perturbation family and prediction-invariance filtering. Geometric perturbations expose substantially greater attribution instability than photometric changes, and without conditioning on prediction preservation, up to 99% of evaluated pairs involve changed predictions. Under this controlled evaluation, we observe consistent method-level trends, with Grad-CAM achieving the highest stability across datasets.

*Ji Young Byun,Young-Jin Park,Jean-Philippe Corbeil,Asma Ben Abacha*

Main category: cs.CV

TL;DR: The paper studies confidence calibration in medical vision-language models (VLMs) for VQA, revealing persistent overconfidence that resists scaling or prompting. Post-hoc calibration (e.g., Platt scaling) reduces calibration error but not AUROC due to monotonicity limits. Incorporating hallucination-detection signals (HAC) improves both calibration and AUROC, especially for open-ended questions. The authors recommend post-hoc calibration as standard practice and show hallucination signals as a practical enhancer for reliable medical VQA.


<details>
  <summary>Details</summary>
Motivation: Medical VLMs must be trusted, not only accurate, as overconfidence can mislead clinicians. There is a lack of systematic study on confidence calibration in medical contexts, despite growing use in clinical decision support.

Method: Empirical evaluation across three VLM families (Qwen3-VL, InternVL3, LLaVA-NeXT), three model scales (2B–38B), and multiple confidence estimation prompting strategies, evaluated on three medical VQA benchmarks. Compared prompting strategies (e.g., chain-of-thought, verbalized confidence) and post-hoc calibration methods (e.g., Platt scaling). Introduced hallucination-aware calibration (HAC) using vision-grounded hallucination signals as auxiliary inputs to refine confidence.

Result: 1) Overconfidence persists across model families and scales, unaffected by prompting or scaling. 2) Post-hoc calibration (e.g., Platt) reduces calibration error and outperforms prompt-based strategies. 3) Due to monotonicity, post-hoc methods cannot improve AUROC; HAC improves both calibration and AUROC, especially for open-ended questions.

Yet, a comprehensive and systematic investigation into the overconfidence of these models remains notably scarce in the medical domain. We address this gap through a comprehensive empirical study of confidence calibration in VLMs, spanning three model families (Qwen3-VL, InternVL3, LLaVA-NeXT), three model scales (2B--38B), and multiple confidence estimation prompting strategies, across three medical visual question answering (VQA) benchmarks. Our study yields three key findings: First, overconfidence persists across model families and is not resolved by scaling or prompting, such as chain-of-thought and verbalized confidence variants. Second, simple post-hoc calibration approaches, such as Platt scaling, reduce calibration error and consistently outperform the prompt-based strategy. Third, due to their (strict) monotonicity, these post-hoc calibration methods are inherently limited in improving the discriminative quality of predictions, leaving AUROC at the same level. Motivated by these findings, we investigate hallucination-aware calibration (HAC), which incorporates vision-grounded hallucination detection signals as complementary inputs to refine confidence estimates. We find that leveraging these hallucination signals improves both calibration and AUROC, with the largest gains on open-ended questions. Overall, our findings suggest post-hoc calibration as standard practice for medical VLM deployment over raw confidence estimates, and highlight the practical usefulness of hallucination signals to enable more reliable use of VLMs in medical VQA.

Furthermore, recognizing that weight elements differ in their relative importance, we adaptively allocate relative importance to each element during SVD process to better preserve accuracy, then extend this framework with quantization applied to both weights and activations, resulting in a highly efficient VLM. Collectively, we introduce~\textit{Weighted SVD} (WSVD), which outperforms other approaches by achieving over $1.8\times$ decoding speedup while preserving accuracy. To address this issue, we introduce a lightweight structural refinement stage between a DETR-style detector and the parser to stabilize the parser interface. Treating raw detector outputs as a compact hypothesis pool, the proposed module performs set-level reasoning over query features, semantic cues, box geometry, and visual evidence. From a shared refined structural state, it jointly determines instance retention, refines box localization, and predicts parser input order before handoff. Method: Augment trajectory prediction with future RGB and depth image generation as dense world-modeling objectives. Abstract: End-to-end autonomous driving models based on Vision-Language-Action (VLA) architectures have shown promising results by learning driving policies through behavior cloning on expert demonstrations. Reinforcement learning (RL) offers a natural remedy by enabling policy exploration beyond the expert distribution. Yet VLA models, typically trained on offline datasets, lack directly observable state transitions, necessitating a learned world model to anticipate action consequences. In this work, we propose a unified understanding-and-generation framework that leverages world modeling to simultaneously enable meaningful exploration and provide dense supervision. We incorporate this exploration signal into a safety-gated reward and optimize the policy via Group Relative Policy Optimization (GRPO). Our results demonstrate that model merging through an optimal checkpoint selection strategy provides an effective approach for building foundation models for multi-resolution data. The model weights, pretraining code, pretraining data, and evaluation code are available at: https://github.com/kerner-lab/MOMO.

Stage II uses a semantics-aware autoregressive model to parse BoxMesh into parametric sewing patterns. Autoregressive models handle variable-length, structured panel configurations and stitching relationships.

In contrast to the well-studied forward process of draping designed sewing patterns using mature physical simulation engines, the inverse process of recovering parametric 2D patterns from deformed garment geometry remains fundamentally ill-posed for existing methods. We propose a two-stage framework that centers on a structured intermediate representation, BoxMesh, which serves as the key to bridging the gap between 3D garment geometry and parametric sewing patterns. BoxMesh encodes both garment-level geometry and panel-level structure in 3D, while explicitly disentangling intrinsic panel geometry and stitching topology from draping-induced deformations. This representation imposes a physically grounded structure on the problem, significantly reducing ambiguity. In Stage I, a geometry-driven autoregressive model infers BoxMesh from the input 3D garment. In Stage II, a semantics-aware autoregressive model parses BoxMesh into parametric sewing patterns. We adopt autoregressive modeling to naturally handle the variable-length and structured nature of panel configurations and stitching relationships. This decomposition separates geometric inversion from structured pattern inference, leading to more accurate and robust recovery. Extensive experiments demonstrate that our method achieves state-of-the-art performance on the GarmentCodeData benchmark and generalizes effectively to real-world scans and single-view images.

In this paper, we provide the first unified perspective on this phenomenon by analyzing its mechanism and implications. We begin by demonstrating that adversarial membership fabrication is consistently effective across diverse architectures and datasets. We then reveal a distinctive geometric signature - a characteristic gradient-norm collapse trajectory - that reliably separates fabricated from true members despite their nearly identical semantic representations. Building on this insight, we introduce a principled detection strategy grounded in gradient-geometry signals and develop a robust inference framework that substantially mitigates adversarial manipulation. Extensive experiments show that fabrication is broadly effective, while our detection and robust inference strategies significantly enhance resilience. This work establishes the first comprehensive framework for adversarial membership manipulation in vision models.

We propose CANDLE (Color Ambient Normalization with DINO Layer Enhancement), which introduces DINO Omni-layer Guidance (D.O.G.) to adaptively inject multi-layer DINOv3 features into successive encoder stages, and a color-frequency refinement design (BFACG + SFFB) to suppress decoder-side chromatic collapse and detail contamination. We introduce LumaFlux, a first physically and perceptually guided diffusion transformer (DiT) for SDR-to-HDR reconstruction by adapting a large pretrained DiT. Our LumaFlux introduces (1) a Physically-Guided Adaptation (PGA) module that injects luminance, spatial descriptors, and frequency cues into attention through low-rank residuals; (2) a Perceptual Cross-Modulation (PCM) layer that stabilizes chroma and texture via FiLM conditioning from vision encoder features; and (3) an HDR Residual Coupler that fuses physical and perceptual signals under a timestep- and layer-adaptive modulation schedule. Finally, a lightweight Rational-Quadratic Spline decoder reconstructs smooth, interpretable tone fields for highlight and exposure expansion, enhancing the output of the VAE decoder to generate HDR. To enable robust HDR learning, we curate the first large-scale SDR-HDR training corpus. For fair and reproducible comparison, we further establish a new evaluation benchmark, comprising HDR references and corresponding expert-graded SDR versions. Across benchmarks, LumaFlux outperforms state-of-the-art baselines, achieving superior luminance reconstruction and perceptual color fidelity with minimal additional parameters.

### [50] [QAPruner: Quantization-Aware Vision Token Pruning for Multimodal Large Language Models](https://arxiv.org/abs/2604.02816)
*Xinhao Wang,Zhonyu Xia,Zhiwei Lin,Zhe Li,Yongtao Wang*

Main category: cs.CV

TL;DR: A quantization-aware vision token pruning framework co-optimizes PTQ and token pruning for low-bit Multimodal LLMs, achieving higher accuracy and beating dense quantization baselines at aggressive pruning.


<details>
  <summary>Details</summary>
Motivation: PTQ and vision token pruning are interdependent in MLLMs; pruning can discard activation outliers essential for numerical stability in low-bit quantization, worsening errors if treated independently.

Method: Introduce a lightweight hybrid sensitivity metric that combines simulated group-wise quantization error with outlier intensity, and fuse it with semantic relevance scores to retain tokens that are both informative and robust to quantization; jointly apply token pruning with PTQ on standard LLaVA architectures.

Result: Experiments show consistent improvement over naive baselines; at a pruning ratio retaining 12.5% of visual tokens, accuracy improves by 2.24% over the baseline and even surpasses dense quantization without pruning.

Conclusion: This work is the first to explicitly co-optimize vision token pruning and PTQ for accurate low-bit MLLM inference, demonstrating effective coupling and practical gains for resource-constrained deployment.

Abstract: Multimodal Large Language Models (MLLMs) have shown strong reasoning ability, but their high computational and memory costs hinder deployment in resource-constrained settings. While Post-Training Quantization (PTQ) and vision token pruning are standard compression techniques, they are usually treated as independent optimizations. In this paper, we show that these two techniques are strongly coupled: naively applying semantic-based token pruning to PTQ-optimized MLLMs can discard activation outliers that are important for numerical stability and thus worsen quantization errors in low-bit regimes (\textit{e.g.}, W4A4). To address this issue, we propose a quantization-aware vision token pruning framework. Our method introduces a lightweight hybrid sensitivity metric that combines simulated group-wise quantization error with outlier intensity. By combining this metric with standard semantic relevance scores, the method retains tokens that are both semantically informative and robust to quantization. Experiments on standard LLaVA architectures show that our method consistently outperforms naive integration baselines. At an aggressive pruning ratio that retains only 12.5\% of visual tokens, our framework improves accuracy by 2.24\% over the baseline and even surpasses dense quantization without pruning. To the best of our knowledge, this is the first method that explicitly co-optimizes vision token pruning and PTQ for accurate low-bit MLLM inference.

To mitigate cross-modal interference, we propose a Bidirectionally Controlled Teacher architecture, which utilizes parallel branches to fully decouple RGB and perception processing and adopts two zero-initialized control links to gradually learn pixel-wise consistency. In Fact-Hash, we project 3D coordinates into multiple lower-dimensional forms (2D or 1D) before applying the hash function and then aggregate them into a single feature. Existing prompt-based approaches use handcrafted or learned prompt embeddings as reference vectors for normal/anomalous states. We propose Sparse-Projected Guides (SPG), a prompt-free framework that learns sparse guide coefficients in the Sparse Autoencoder (SAE) latent space, which generate normal/anomaly guide vectors via the SAE dictionary. SPG employs a two stage learning strategy on the labeled auxiliary dataset: (i) train an SAE on patch-token features, and (ii) optimize only guide coefficients using auxiliary pixel-level masks while freezing the backbone and SAE. On MVTec AD and VisA under cross-dataset zero-shot settings, SPG achieves competitive image-level detection and strong pixel-level segmentation; with DINOv3, SPG attains the highest pixellevel AUROC among the compared methods. We also report SPG instantiated with OpenCLIP (ViT-L/14@336px) to align the backbone with CLIP-based baselines. Moreover, the learned guide coefficients trace decisions back to a small set of dictionary atoms, revealing category-general and category-specific factors.

### [62] [Unlocking Positive Transfer in Incrementally Learning Surgical Instruments: A Self-reflection Hierarchical Prompt Framework](https://arxiv.org/abs/2604.02877)
*Yu Zhu,Kang Li,Zheng Li,Pheng-Ann Heng*

<details>
  <summary>Details</summary>
Motivation: To address catastrophic forgetting and underutilization of past knowledge in progressive learning for surgical instrument segmentation, by exploiting both forward transfer (past knowledge aiding new classes) and backward transfer (new learning refining past knowledge).

Method: Freeze a pre-trained backbone and incrementally append instrument-aware prompts for new classes. Organize prompts into a hierarchical prompt parsing tree: root is instrument-shared prompts, intermediate n-part-shared prompts, and leaf instrument-distinct prompts. Applicable to CNNs and transformer-based foundation models.

Result: Reported improvements of over 5% (CNN-based) and over 11% (transformer-based) over competing methods on two public benchmarks.

Conclusion: The framework jointly enables positive forward and backward knowledge transfer in class incremental segmentation for surgical instruments, improving adaptability and robustness while remaining compatible with both CNNs and foundation-model architectures.

Abstract: To continuously enhance model adaptability in surgical video scene parsing, recent studies incrementally update it to progressively learn to segment an increasing number of surgical instruments over time. However, prior works constantly overlooked the potential of positive forward knowledge transfer, i.e., how past knowledge could help learn new classes, and positive backward knowledge transfer, i.e., how learning new classes could help refine past knowledge. In this paper, we propose a self-reflection hierarchical prompt framework that unlocks the power of positive forward and backward knowledge transfer in class incremental segmentation, aiming to proficiently learn new instruments, improve existing skills of regular instruments, and avoid catastrophic forgetting of old instruments. Our framework is built on a frozen, pre-trained model that adaptively appends instrument-aware prompts for new classes throughout training episodes. To enable positive forward knowledge transfer, we organize instrument prompts into a hierarchical prompt parsing tree with the instrument-shared prompt partition as the root node, n-part-shared prompt partitions as intermediate nodes and instrument-distinct prompt partitions as leaf nodes, to expose the reusable historical knowledge for new classes to simplify their learning. Conversely, to encourage positive backward knowledge transfer, we conduct self-reflection refining on existing knowledge by directed-weighted graph propagation, examining the knowledge associations recorded in the tree to improve its representativeness without causing catastrophic forgetting. Our framework is applicable to both CNN-based models and advanced transformer-based foundation models, yielding more than 5% and 11% improvements over the competing methods on two public benchmarks respectively.

### [64] [Information-Regularized Constrained Inversion for Stable Avatar Editing from Sparse Supervision](https://arxiv.org/abs/2604.02883)
*Zhenxiao Liang,Qixing Huang*

Main category: cs.CV

TL;DR: A conditioning-guided, low-dimensional edit subspace approach for editing animatable human avatars from sparse supervision, improving stability and reducing identity leakage and temporal flicker by constrained inversion in a structured latent space.


<details>
  <summary>Details</summary>
Motivation: Ill-posed edits under sparse supervision cause identity leakage and temporal flicker due to insufficient information to determine edit directions. The paper argues for a better-conditioned inversion by restricting updates to a dedicated edit subspace and leveraging a conditioning objective.

Method: Construct a low-dimensional, part-specific edit subspace within the avatar latent space. Inversion uses a conditioning objective derived from a local linearization of the decode-render pipeline to create an edit-subspace information matrix. The spectrum of this matrix informs stability and drives frame reweighting and keyframe activation. Computation relies on Hessian-vector products to keep operations on small subspaces.

Result: The approach yields improved stability under limited edited supervision, reducing unintended identity changes and temporal flicker by solving a constrained, well-conditioned inversion.

Conclusion: Conditioning-guided, subspace-constrained inversion enables reliable edits with sparse supervision in avatar editing by limiting updates to a structured, informative subspace and by predicting stability via the edit-subspace information matrix.

Abstract: Editing animatable human avatars typically relies on sparse supervision, often a few edited keyframes, yet naively fitting a reconstructed avatar to these edits frequently causes identity leakage and pose-dependent temporal flicker. We argue that these failures are best understood as an ill-conditioned inversion: the available edited constraints do not sufficiently determine the latent directions responsible for the intended edit. We propose a conditioning-guided edited reconstruction framework that performs editing as a constrained inversion in a structured avatar latent space, restricting updates to a low-dimensional, part-specific edit subspace to prevent unintended identity changes. Crucially, we design the editing constraints during inversion by optimizing a conditioning objective derived from a local linearization of the full decoding-and-rendering pipeline, yielding an edit-subspace information matrix whose spectrum predicts stability and drives frame reweighting / keyframe activation. The resulting method operates on small subspace matrices and can be implemented efficiently (e.g., via Hessian-vector products), and improves stability under limited edited supervision.

  <summary>Details</summary>

A dedicated, efficient, and perceptually aligned evaluation framework for image fusion is needed.

Method: A divide-and-conquer approach with a lightweight network that approximates common metrics. The fused image is decomposed into infrared and visible components, and the evaluation model assesses information preservation in these components. Additionally, a consistency evaluation framework is proposed to align fusion metrics with human perception, using independent no-reference scores and downstream task performance as references.

To address these issues, we propose a unified evaluation framework specifically tailored for image fusion. At its core is a lightweight network designed efficiently to approximate widely used metrics, following a divide-and-conquer strategy. Unlike conventional approaches that directly assess similarity between fused and source images, we first decompose the fusion result into infrared and visible components. The evaluation model is then used to measure the degree of information preservation in these separated components, effectively disentangling the fusion evaluation process. During training, we incorporate a contrastive learning strategy and inform our evaluation model by perceptual scene assessment provided by a large language model. Last, we propose the first consistency evaluation framework, which measures the alignment between image fusion metrics and human visual perception, using both independent no-reference scores and downstream tasks performance as objective references. Extensive experiments show that our learning-based evaluation paradigm delivers both superior efficiency (up to 1,000 times faster) and greater consistency across a range of standard image fusion benchmarks. Our code will be publicly available at https://github.com/AWCXV/EvaNet.

TL;DR: MMTalker is a 3D audio-driven facial animation framework that uses multi-resolution mesh representation, differentiable sampling, residual GCNs, and dual cross-attention for robust multimodal fusion, achieving improved lip-sync and eye-movement realism.


<details>
  <summary>Details</summary>
Motivation: To overcome the ill-posed cross-modal mapping from speech to 3D facial motion, which degrades lip-sync accuracy and realism. The work aims to provide a continuous, detailed 3D face representation and effective multimodal fusion to improve synchronization and expressiveness.

Method: 1) Continuous 3D face representation via mesh parameterization linking UV space to 3D mesh; non-uniform differentiable sampling with learnable per-triangle sampling probabilities for fine-grained detail. 2) Residual graph convolutional network and dual cross-attention to extract discriminative facial motion features from multiple modalities, leveraging hierarchical speech features and explicit spatiotemporal mesh features for multimodal fusion. 3) Lightweight regression network predicts vertex-wise displacements by jointly processing sampled UV points and encoded facial motion features.

Result: Experiments show significant improvements over state-of-the-art methods, particularly in lip-sync accuracy and eye movement synchronization, indicating more realistic and synchronized 3D talking faces.

Conclusion: The integration of multi-resolution mesh representation, differentiable sampling, and dual cross-attention multimodal fusion in MMTalker yields accurate, high-detail 3D facial motion with improved lip-sync and expressive realism.

Abstract: Speech-driven three-dimensional (3D) facial animation synthesis aims to build a mapping from one-dimensional (1D) speech signals to time-varying 3D facial motion signals. Current methods still face challenges in maintaining lip-sync accuracy and producing realistic facial expressions, primarily due to the highly ill-posed nature of this cross-modal mapping. In this paper, we introduce a novel 3D audio-driven facial animation synthesis method through multi-resolution representation and multi-modal feature fusion, called MMTalker which can accurately reconstruct the rich details of 3D facial motion.
  We first achieve the continuous representation of 3D face with details by mesh parameterization and non-uniform differentiable sampling. The mesh parameterization technique establishes the correspondence between UV plane and 3D facial mesh and is used to offer ground truth for the continuous learning. Differentiable non-uniform sampling enables precise facial detail acquisition by setting learnable sampling probability in each triangular face. Next, we employ residual graph convolutional network and dual cross-attention mechanism to extract discriminative facial motion feature from multiple input modalities. This proposed multimodal fusion strategy takes full use of the hierarchical features of speech and the explicit spatiotemporal geometric features of facial mesh. Finally, a lightweight regression network predicts the vertex-wise geometric displacements of the synthesized talking face by jointly processing the sampled points in the canonical UV space and the encoded facial motion features.
  Comprehensive experiments demonstrate that significant improvements are achieved over state-of-the-art methods, especially in the synchronization accuracy of lip and eye movements.

*Koshiro Nagano,Ryo Fujii,Ryo Hachiuma,Fumiaki Sato,Taiki Sekii,Hideo Saito*

Main category: cs.CV

  <summary>Details</summary>
Motivation: Existing data-synthesis approaches often enhance robustness only indirectly through sample diversification and may learn spurious correlations from synthesis biases and artifacts; there is a need for supervision that explicitly emphasizes target regions during discrimination.

Method: During synthesis, provenance information indicates whether input-space regions originate from the target object. Input gradients are decomposed using this provenance (target vs non-target) and gradient guidance is applied to suppress non-target gradients, yielding auxiliary supervision that focuses representation learning on target regions.

Result: The method demonstrates effectiveness and generality across multiple tasks and modalities (weakly supervised object localization, spatio-temporal action localization, and image classification), indicating improved emphasis on true target regions and reduced reliance on synthesis artifacts.

Conclusion: Incorporating provenance-derived gradient guidance directly targets discriminative regions, enabling more robust, region-focused representations and broad applicability across vision tasks that rely on synthetic data.

Abstract: Learning methods using synthetic data have attracted attention as an effective approach for increasing the diversity of training data while reducing collection costs, thereby improving the robustness of model discrimination. However, many existing methods improve robustness only indirectly through the diversification of training samples and do not explicitly teach the model which regions in the input space truly contribute to discrimination; consequently, the model may learn spurious correlations caused by synthesis biases and artifacts. Motivated by this limitation, this paper proposes a learning framework that uses provenance information obtained during the training data synthesis process, indicating whether each region in the input space originates from the target object, as an auxiliary supervisory signal to promote the acquisition of representations focused on target regions. Specifically, input gradients are decomposed based on information about target and non-target regions during synthesis, and input gradient guidance is introduced to suppress gradients over non-target regions. This suppresses the model's reliance on non-target regions and directly promotes the learning of discriminative representations for target regions. Experiments demonstrate the effectiveness and generality of the proposed method across multiple tasks and modalities, including weakly supervised object localization, spatio-temporal action localization, and image classification.

### [77] [Collaborative Multi-Mode Pruning for Vision-Language Models](https://arxiv.org/abs/2604.02956)
*Zimeng Wu,Yunhong Wang,Donghao Wang,Jiaxin Chen*

Main category: cs.CV

TL;DR: CoMP jointly prunes parameters and tokens in vision-language models to maintain performance at high pruning ratios; introduces Collaborative Importance Metric (CIM) and Multi-Mode Pruning Strategy (MPS) for adaptive, staged pruning with historical cost and exploration.


<details>
  <summary>Details</summary>
Motivation: VLMs are large and resource-intensive. Prior pruning methods focus on a single mode (parameters or tokens), which under-utilizes redundancy and degrades performance at aggressive pruning. A joint, adaptive approach can better exploit interdependencies between parameters and tokens.

Method: CIM estimates parameter and token importance by accounting for their mutual interference and the influence of pruned parameters on token scores. MPS decomposes pruning into stages, estimating priors for different pruning modes based on cost and adaptively selecting the optimal mode; incorporates historical cost and random exploration to stabilize pruning and avoid local optima.

Result: Extensive experiments across vision-language tasks and models show CoMP outperforms state-of-the-art single-mode pruning at high pruning ratios, demonstrating improved performance retention. Code is released at the provided GitHub link.

Conclusion: Collaborative multi-mode pruning effectively preserves performance under aggressive pruning in VLMs, validating joint pruning of parameters and tokens as a viable strategy for resource-constrained deployment.

Abstract: Vision-Language Models (VLMs) have advanced rapidly within the unified Transformer architecture, yet their deployment on resource-constrained devices remains challenging due to high computational complexity. While pruning has emerged as an effective technique for compressing VLMs, existing approaches predominantly focus on a single mode by pruning either parameters or tokens, neglecting fully exploring the inherent redundancy in each mode, which leads to substantial performance degradation at high pruning ratios. To address the above limitations, we propose Collaborative Multi-Mode Pruning (CoMP), a novel framework tailored for VLMs by performing joint parameter and token pruning. Specifically, we first design a Collaborative Importance Metric (CIM) that investigates the mutual interference between the coupled parameters and tokens. It incorporates distinct significance of tokens into the computation of parameter importance scores, while simultaneously mitigating the affect of pruned parameters on token importance scores. Moreover, we develop a Multi-Mode Pruning Strategy (MPS) that decomposes the overall pruning process into a sequence of pruning stages, while in each stage we estimate the priory of different pruning modes based on their pruning cost and adaptively shift to the optimal one. Additionally, MPS integrates the historical cost and random exploration, in order to achieve a stable pruning process and avoid local optimum. Extensive experiments across various vision-language tasks and models demonstrate that our method effectively promotes the performance under high pruning ratios by comparing to the state-of-the-art approaches. The source code is available at https://github.com/Wuzimeng/CoMP.git.

### [81] [Effect of Input Resolution on Retinal Vessel Segmentation Performance: An Empirical Study Across Five Datasets](https://arxiv.org/abs/2604.02977)
*Amarnath R*

Main category: cs.CV

TL;DR: Downsampling retinal images can harm thin vessel detection even if Dice scores remain stable. A width-stratified sensitivity analysis shows opposing effects across datasets: high-res datasets benefit from downsampling toward the encoder's operating range for thin vessels, while low-to-mid-res datasets lose thin-vessel sensitivity with any downsampling.


<details>
  <summary>Details</summary>
Motivation: To assess how resizing fundus images for memory constraints affects the detection of thin retinal vessels, and to evaluate whether Dice is a sufficient metric for microvascular segmentation.

Method: Train a baseline UNet on five fundus datasets (DRIVE, STARE, CHASE_DB1, HRF, FIVES) at multiple downsampling ratios with fixed settings. Introduce a width-stratified sensitivity metric that splits vessels into thin (width <3 px), medium (3–7 px), and thick (>7 px) using native widths estimated from a Euclidean distance transform. Compare sensitivity across resolutions and datasets, alongside Dice scores.

Result: Thin-vessel sensitivity on high-resolution datasets (HRF, FIVES) increases as images are downsampled toward the encoder’s operating range, peaking for processed widths 256–876 px. For lower-resolution datasets (DRIVE, STARE, CHASE_DB1), thin-vessel sensitivity is highest near native resolution and declines with downsampling. Across all datasets, aggressive downsampling reduces thin-vessel sensitivity by up to 15.8 percentage points while Dice scores remain relatively stable, indicating Dice alone underestimates microvascular loss.

Conclusion: Dice is insufficient for evaluating microvascular segmentation. Thin-vessel detection is affected by resizing, and width-aware metrics reveal losses not captured by Dice. Practical implications include preserving native or near-native resolution for thin vessels or adopting width-stratified evaluation and memory-aware architectures that maintain subpixel vessel information.

Abstract: Most deep learning pipelines for retinal vessel segmentation resize fundus images to satisfy GPU memory constraints and enable uniform batch processing. However, the impact of this resizing on thin vessel detection remains underexplored. When high resolution images are downsampled, thin vessels are reduced to subpixel structures, causing irreversible information loss even before the data enters the network. Standard volumetric metrics such as the Dice score do not capture this loss because thick vessel pixels dominate the evaluation. We investigated this effect by training a baseline UNet at multiple downsampling ratios across five fundus datasets (DRIVE, STARE, CHASE_DB1, HRF, and FIVES) with native widths ranging from 565 to 3504 pixels, keeping all other settings fixed. We introduce a width-stratified sensitivity metric that evaluates thin (half-width <3 pixels), medium (3 to 7 pixels), and thick (>7 pixels) vessel detection separately, using native resolution width estimates derived from a Euclidean distance transform. Results show that for high-resolution datasets (HRF, FIVES), thin vessel sensitivity improves monotonically as images are downsampled toward the encoder's effective operating range, peaking at processed widths between 256 and 876 pixels. For low-to-mid resolution datasets (DRIVE, STARE, CHASE_DB1), thin vessel sensitivity is highest at or near native resolution and degrades with any downsampling. Across all five datasets, aggressive downsampling reduced thin vessel sensitivity by up to 15.8 percentage points (DRIVE) while Dice remained relatively stable, confirming that Dice alone is insufficient for evaluating microvascular segmentation.

### [82] [Not All Frames Deserve Full Computation: Accelerating Autoregressive Video Generation via Selective Computation and Predictive Extrapolation](https://arxiv.org/abs/2604.02979)
*Hanshuai Cui,Zhiqing Tang,Zhi Yao,Fanshuai Meng,Weijia Jia,Wei Zhao*
